                     <orth orig="Ba" lang="ar" marker="qara3a">قَرَرَ</orth>
                  </form>; (S, M, Msb, K;) but the former is the more usual, or common; (M, TA;) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">قَرَارٌ</foreign>, (S, M, Mgh, K,) of both verbs, (S,) or this is a simple subst., (Msb,) and <foreign lang="ar">قُرُورٌ</foreign>, (S, M, K,) of the former verb, (S,) and <foreign lang="ar">قَرٌّ</foreign> (M, Msb, K) and <foreign lang="ar">تَقِرَّةٌ</foreign>, (M, K,) which last is anomalous, (M,) and <foreign lang="ar">تَقْرَارَةٌ</foreign>; (TA;) and

      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n35340-2" target="تقارَّ" n="2" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>, (S, M, K,) originally <foreign lang="ar">تَقَارَرَ</foreign>, (TA,) <foreign lang="ar">فِيهِ</foreign>; (S, TA;) and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n35340-3" target="تقرّر" n="3" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>; (TA;) [and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n35340-4" target="اقترّ" n="4" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>, as appears from an ex. below;] <hi rend="ital">He,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it, settled; became firm, steady, fixed, settled,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">established; became motionless, stationary, standing, quiet, still,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">at rest; rested; remained; continued; resided; in the place;</hi> syn. <foreign lang="ar">ثَبَتَ وَسَكَنَ</foreign>, (K,) and <foreign lang="ar">تَمَكَّنَ</foreign> [which, when said of a man, particularly implies being <hi rend="ital">in authority and power</hi>]. (Msb.) [See also 4.] In the words of the Kur, [xxxiii. 33,] <foreign lang="ar">وَقِرْنَ فِى</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">بُيُوتِكُنَّ</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">وَقَرْنَ</foreign>, [<hi rend="ital">And remain ye in your houses,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">chambers,</hi>] <foreign lang="ar">قِرْنَ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">قَرْنَ</foreign> are contractions of <foreign lang="ar">اِقْرِرْنَ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">اِقْرَرْنَ</foreign> like as <foreign lang="ar">ظِلْنَ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">ظَلْنَ</foreign> are contractions of <foreign lang="ar">اِظْلِلْنَ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">اِظْلَلْنَ</foreign>: (M, Bd, * TA: * [but see <foreign lang="ar">ظَلَّ</foreign>:]) or <foreign lang="ar">قِرْنَ</foreign> is from <foreign lang="ar">وَقَرَ</foreign>, aor.      
    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Bi" lang="ar" marker="qari3a">قَرِرَ</orth>
                  </form>, inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">وَقَارٌ</foreign>; (Bd, TA; *) and <foreign lang="ar">قَرْنَ</foreign> from <foreign lang="ar">قَارَ</foreign>, aor. <foreign lang="ar">يَقَارُ</foreign>, signifying <foreign lang="ar">اِجْتَمَعَ</foreign>. (Bd.) It is said in a proverb, <foreign lang="ar">اِبْدَأْهُمْ بِالصُّرَاخِ يَقِرُّوا</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Begin thou by crying out to them,</hi> and <hi rend="ital">they will become still,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">quiet;</hi> or] begin thou by complaining of them, and they will be content to be still, or quiet. (TA.) [But see Freytag's Arab. Prov., i. 173, where, instead of <foreign lang="ar">يَقِرُّوا</foreign>, we find <foreign lang="ar">يَفِرُّوا</foreign>.] You also say <foreign lang="ar">فُلَانٌ مَا <ref cref="n35340-5" target="يَتَقَارُّ" n="5" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>فِى مَكَانِهِ</foreign>, i. e.   
      <foreign lang="ar">مَا <ref cref="n35340-6" target="يَسْتَقِرُّ" n="6" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Such a one does not rest,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">remain, in his place</hi>]. (S.) And it is said in a trad. of Aboo-Dharr, <foreign lang="ar">فَلَمْ <ref cref="n35340-7" target="أَتَقَارَّ" n="7" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>أَنْ قُمْتُ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">And I did not delay to rise,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">stand up.</hi> (TA.) You say also, of a woman, <foreign lang="ar">تَقِرُّ لِمَا يُصْنَعُ بِهَا</foreign> (K) <hi rend="ital">She suffers quietly what is done to her,</hi> such as the being kissed, &amp;c. (K. * TA.) And <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n35340-8" target="اِقْتَرَّ" n="8" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>مَآءُ الفَحْلِ فِى الرَّحِمِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">The seed of the stallion rested,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">remained, in the womb</hi> (S, K) of the she-camel; (K;) <hi rend="ital">i. q.</hi>   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n35340-9" target="استقرّ" n="9" type="1" subtype="SO" lang="ar"/></foreign>. (S, K.) See also <foreign lang="ar">قَرٌّ</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">قَرَارٌ</foreign>, below.       <sense type="A" n="2">-A2-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">قَرَّ</foreign>, (S, M, Mgh, Msb, K,) like <foreign lang="ar">لَبِسَ</foreign> (Mgh) and <foreign lang="ar">تَعِبَ</foreign>, (Msb,) [so that the second pers. is <foreign lang="ar">قَرِرْتَ</foreign>,] aor.

    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Bi" lang="ar" marker="qari3a">قَرِرَ</orth>

    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Bu" lang="ar" marker="qaru3a">قَرُرَ</orth>
                  </form>; (Lh, M, K;) or, accord. to MF, Lh mentions the aors.      
    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Bu" lang="ar" marker="qaru3a">قَرُرَ</orth>
                  </form> and      
    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Bi" lang="ar" marker="qari3a">قَرِرَ</orth>
                  </form> in his Nawádir; and IKtt, the three forms of aor., and so the author of the Ma'álim; but IKtt says, in his Kitáb el-Abniyeh, <foreign lang="ar">يَقَرُّ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">يَقِرُّ</foreign>, though he may have mentioned the three forms in another book; and accord. to what is stated [in the M and] in the L, Lh says <foreign lang="ar">يَقُرُّ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">يَقَرُّ</foreign>, which is a rare form; (TA;) [on which it should be remarked, that ISd, IKtt, and Mtr, mention the form      
    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Ba" lang="ar" marker="qara3a">قَرَرَ</orth>

                  <form>       
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">قَرَارِىٌّ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form>, from <foreign lang="ar">قَرَارٌ</foreign>, because he who is so called remains in the dwellings, (TA,) <hi rend="ital">An inhabitant of a region, district,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">tract, of cities, towns,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">villages, and of cultivated land, who does not go in search of pasture:</hi> (K:) <hi rend="ital">a tailor:</hi> (IAar, S, K:) <hi rend="ital">a butcher:</hi> or <hi rend="ital">any workman</hi> or <hi rend="ital">artificer.</hi> (K.) The vulgar use it in the present day as an intensive epithet; saying <foreign lang="ar">خَيَّاط قَرَارِى</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">نَجَّار</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">قَرَارِى</foreign>, (TA,) meaning <hi rend="ital">a clever tailor,</hi> and <hi rend="ital">a clever carpenter;</hi> and in like manner, <foreign lang="ar">قِرْقَارِى</foreign>.                      <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">قَارُورَةٌ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form> [<hi rend="ital">A flask, bottle,</hi> or, as it generally signifies in the present day, <hi rend="ital">phial;</hi>] the <hi rend="ital">thing in which wine,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">beverage, &amp;c.,</hi> (M,) or <hi rend="ital">in which wine,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">beverage, and the like,</hi> (K,) <hi rend="ital">rests,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">remains:</hi> (M, K:) or it is <hi rend="ital">of glass,</hi> (S, M, K,) only; (M, K;) <hi rend="ital">a kind of vessel of glass:</hi> (Msb:) pl. <foreign lang="ar">قَوَارِيرُ</foreign>. (S, &amp;c.) The dim. is <foreign lang="ar">قُوَيْرِيرَةٌ</foreign>. (TA.) <foreign lang="ar">قَوَارِيرَ قَوَارِيرَ مِنْ فِضَّةٍ</foreign>, in the Kur, [lxxvi. 15 and 16,] is said by some learned men to mean <hi rend="ital">Vessels,</hi> [<hi rend="ital">vessels</hi>] <hi rend="ital">white as silver and clear as</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">قوارير</foreign>. <pb n="2502"/> [See also art. <foreign lang="ar">فض</foreign>.] An <foreign lang="ar">ا</foreign> is added by some to the final <foreign lang="ar">قوارير</foreign> [of verse 15] in order that the ends of the verses may be similar. (M.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  <hi rend="ital">A receptacle for fresh, or dried, dates;</hi> also called <foreign lang="ar">قَوْصَرَةٌ</foreign>. (Msb.)          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  The <hi rend="ital">black of the eye;</hi> the <hi rend="ital">part, of the eye, that is surrounded by the white:</hi> (M, K:) as being likened to <foreign lang="ar">قارورة</foreign> of glass, because of its clearness, and because the observer sees his image in it. (M, TA.) [See an ex. in a verse cited in the first paragraph of art. <foreign lang="ar">سلب</foreign>.]          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">A woman,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">wife;</hi> as also <foreign lang="ar">قَوْصَرَّةٌ</foreign>: (Az, Msb:) called by the former appellation because the child, or the seed, rests in her womb, as a thing rests in a vessel, and as being likened to a vessel of glass because of her weakness. (Msb.) Hence the words [of Mohammad] in a trad., <foreign lang="ar">رُوَيْدَكَ رِفْقًا بِٱلْقَوَارِيرِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Go thou leisurely: act gently with the</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">قَوَارير</foreign>]: women being here likened to <foreign lang="ar">قوارير</foreign> of glass because of their weakness of purpose, and their fickleness; for such vessels are soon broken and cannot be restored to soundness: meaning, that the man thus addressed, named <foreign lang="ar">أَنْجَشَة</foreign> (Anjesheh), [a freedman of Mohammad,] should not raise his voice and sing in driving the camels, for fear of the women's having their desires excited by what they heard; or for fear that the camels, hearing the singing, should go quickly, and jolt and fatigue the riders.
